Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Atharvan.тАФekaс╣гaс╣гс╣нi. yamadevatyam mantroktabahudevatyaс╣Б ca (41-43. sarasvat─лdevaty─Бs; 40. r─Бudr─л; 44-46. mantroktapitс╣Ыdevaty─Бs; 51, 52. pitrye). tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 8, 15. ─Бrс╣г─л pan╠Дkti; 14, 49, 50. bhurij; 18-20, 21-23. jagat─л; 37, 38. paroс╣гс╣Зih; 56, 57, 61. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 59. pur─Бbс╣Ыhat─л.]

Whitney

Comment

тМКOnly one verse (46) is found in P─Бipp., and that in book ii. Only four s┼лtras of the V─Бit. cite verses from this hymn, and those verses are 44-46, 51, and 55. In the K─Бu┼Ы., as already noted by Whitney, p. 814, nearly all the verses from 1. 40 to the end of the book have their uses in the ritual. That Parts I. and II. and III. of the hymn as divided below are utterly impertinent to the proper subject of the book and therefore without ritual application, is a fact on which Weber, Sb. 1895, p. 819, has already animadverted.тМЛ

тМКA clear synoptic statement of the provenience of the different groups of verses, or of the single verses, that enter into the composition of this hymn appears so desirable for the critical study thereof, that I subjoin the following:

тМКIt thus appears that every verse of our hymn has its correspondent in the RV. save four (or five, if one wishes to count vs. 57): to wit, vs. 17, which is not found to my knowledge in any other text; vss. 27, 28, repeated from AV. vii. (see above); and vs. 61, found in SV.тМЛ

Griffith

An accompaniment to funeral ceremonies and sacrificial offerings to ancestral spirits

режрез рдУ рдЪрд┐рддреНрд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдВрд╕рдЦреНрдпрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Unto a friend would I turn with friendship; having gone through much
    ocean, may the pious one take a grandson of [his] father, considering
    further onward upon the earth (kс╣г├бm).
Notes

That is, ‘making thoughtful provision for the future.’ The verse is,
without variant, RV. x. 10. 1. Our Bs.E. have pur├║ in saс╣Бhit─Б. The
verse is also SV. i. 340, which has a considerably different text: for
a, ─Б╠Б tv─Б s├бkh─Бyaс╕е sakhy─Б╠Б vavс╣Ыtyus; in b, arс╣Зav─Б╠Бс╣Е jagamy─Бс╕е;
for d, asm├нn kс╣г├бye pratar─Б╠Бс╣Б d─л╠Бdy─Бnaс╕е. The comm. takes vavс╣Ыty─Бm
as of causative value, = vartay─Бmi: d─лdhy─Бnas he explains first (as
if it were d─лdy─Бnas) by d─лpyam─Бnas, ‘becoming illustrious over the
whole earth’; but also, alternatively, by “thinking [upon a means of
impregnating me]."тАФThe word sakhy─Б╠Б he takes as instr. of sakhy─Б╠Б
‘friendship’ тМКso Lanman, Noun-Inflection, JAOS. x. 336тМЛ, and renders
by sakhitvena; but also alternatively as instr. of sakh─л, ‘by means
of a female friend,’ a go-between!

тМКAn oxytone feminine stem sakh─л╠Б corresponding (cf. JAOS. x. 368) to a
barytone masculine s├бkhi should accent its instr. sakhy─Б╠А (JAOS. x.
368, top, 381), not sakhy─Б╠Б.тМЛ тМКAufrecht, Festgruss an B├╢htlingk,
1888, page 1, took sakhy─Б╠Б as a dative of sakhy├б; and Pischel, Ved.
Stud. i. 65 (title-page dated 1889), made a cogent and interesting
argument against my view and came (independently, without doubt) to the
same conclusion as Aufrecht.тАФFor Geldner’s interpretation of the whole
verse, see Gurup┼лj─Бkaumud─л, p. 19-20.тМЛ

Griffith

Fain would I win my friend to kindly friendship. So may the Sage, come through the air’s wide ocean, Remembering the earth and days to follow, obtain a son the issue of his father.

режреи рди рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thy friend wants (va┼Ы) not that friendship of thine, that she of
    like sign should become of diverse form; the sons of the great Asura,
    heroes, sustainers of the sky (d├нv), look widely about.
Notes

That is, Varuna’s spies are on the watch against such unpermitted acts.
Our Bp.Bs. read in b s├бlakс╣гmy─Б. The comm. understands salakс╣гm─Б
as ekodaratvalakс╣гaс╣Зaс╣Б yasy─Бс╕е ‘marked as from the same womb,’ and
viс╣гur┼лp─Б as “changing from sister to wife.” The same expression occurs
below in 1. 34, and variations of it in TS. i. 3. 10┬╣ (quoted further at
vi. 3. 11┬▓) and MS. i. 2. 17 (a passage corresponding to, but different
from, that in TS.); also VS. vi. 20 b (do.). It seems to have a kind
of proverbial currency, as applied to things that change from one
character to another. The comm. renders pari khyan by pari vadanti
or nir─Бkariс╣гyanti. The verse is RV. x. 10. 2.

Griffith

Thy friend loves not the friendship which considers her who is near in kindred as a stranger. Sons of the mighty Asura, the heroes, supporters of the heaven, see far around them.

Yea, this the Immortals seek of thee with longing, a scion of the only man existing. Then let thy soul and mine be knit together. Embrace thy con- sort as her loving husband.

Griffith

Shall we do now what we ne’er did aforetime? we who spoke righteously now talk impurely? Gandharva in the floods, the Dame of Waters–such is our bond, such our most lofty kinship.

Griffith

Even in the womb God Tvashtar, vivifier, shaping all forms, Creator, made us consorts. Ne’er are his holy statutes violated: that we are his the heaven and earth acknowledge.

Griffith

Who yokes to-day unto the pole of Order the strong and passio- nate steers of checkless spirit, With shaft-armed mouths, heart-piercing, joy-bestowing? Long shall he live who duly pays them service.

Translation
  1. Who knows of that first day? who saw it? who shall proclaim it here?
    Great is the ordinance (dh─Б╠Бman) of Mitra, of Varuс╣Зa; why, O lustful
    one, wilt thou speak to men with deceit (? v─л╠Бci)?

adj. meaning vividham a├▒canto gacchantaс╕е saс╣Бcarantaс╕е, and qualifying

Gurup┼лj─Бkaumud─л, p. 21-22.тМЛ

Griffith

Who knows that earliest day whereof thou speakest, Who hath beheld it? Who can here declare it? Great is the law of Varuna and Mitra. What, wanton, wilt thou say to men to tempt them?

Whitney
Translation
  1. Desire of Yama hath come unto me Yam─л, in order to lying together in
    the same lair (y├│ni); I would fain yield (ric) my body, as wife to
    husband; may we whirl off, like two chariot wheels.
Notes

That is, probably, like the wheels of two chariots interlocked with each
other in battle. RV. x. 10. 7 has no variants from our text. The comm.
makes v├н vс╣Ыheva mean saс╣Б┼Ыleс╣гaс╣Б karav─Бva, adding itaretarayoс╕е
saс╣Б┼Ыleс╣гo vivarh─Б; and his first explanation of rathy─Б is as =
rathyay─Б ‘on the carriage road’! Our P.M.I. accent vс╣Ыh├йva. The
metrical definition of the Anukr. as pan╠Дkti is very strange, though
the verse can be reduced to 40 syllables by refusing to make ordinary
resolutions.

Griffith

Yami am possessed by love of Yama, that I may rest on the same couch beside him. I as a wife would yield me to my husband. Like car-wheels let us speed to meet each other.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They stand not, they wink not, those spies of the gods who go about
    here; with another than me, O lustful one, go quickly; with him whirl
    off like two chariot wheels.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 10. 8, without variant. The comm. reads eke at end
of a; he explains t┼л╠Бyam in c by t┼лrс╣Зam, and supplies
ramasva: ‘hasten to enjoy thyself.’

Griffith

They stand not still, they never close their eyelids, those senti- nels of Gods who wander round us. Not me–go quickly, wanton, with another, and hasten like a chariot-wheel to meet him.

  1. By nights, by days one may pay reverence (da┼Ыasy) to him; the

Notes

RV. x. 10. 9 differs from our text only by reading in d bibhс╣Ыy─Бt;
and this reading the translation implies, vivс╣Ыh─Бt seeming
unexplainable save as a corruption, suggested by the forms of vi-vс╣Ыh
in the two preceding verses. The connection of the verse is very loose,
and the sense of b especially doubtful. One is tempted to emend to
mim─лly─Бt; but ─Б╠Б mim─лy─Бt is found in TB. iii. 6. 13 тМК2d pr─Бiс╣гaтМЛ,
explained by its commentary as meaning ─Бgatya pravi┼Ыeyuс╕е. Our comm.
explains? ├║n m- as ├║rdhvaс╣Б gacchet (the RV. comm. as ud etu). Our
comm. further reads at the end aj─Бmis, and understands it of Yam─л. The
adjectives in c are dual; the comm. supplies “earth with heaven and
heaven with earth.” тМКCf. Weber, Sb., p. 823.тМЛ

Griffith

May Surya’s eye with days and nights endow him, and ever may his light spread out before him. In heaven and earth the kindred pair commingle. On Yami be the unbrotherly act of Yama.

Translation
  1. Verily there shall come those later ages (yug├б) in which next of
    kin (j─Бm├н) shall do what is unkinly тМК├бj─БmiтМЛ. Put thine arm
    underneath a hero (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б); seek, O fortunate one, another husband
    than me.
Notes

The verse is, without variant, RV. x. 10. 10. Upa barbс╣Ыhi in c
means ‘make an upab├бrhaс╣Зa (cushion, pillow) of.’ Our comm. regards the
anomalous barbс╣Ыhi тМКGram. ┬з 1011 aтМЛ as barbс╣Ы + hi, -bс╣Ы- being
for -bс╣Ыh- by Vedic license.

Griffith

Sure there will come succeeding times when brothers and sisters will do acts unmeet for kinsfolk. Not me, O fair one–seek another husband, and make thine arm a pillow for thy consort.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What should brother be when there is no protector? or what sister,
    when destruction impends (ni-gam)? Impelled by desire, I prate thus
    much; mingle thou thy body with my body.
Notes

The first half-verse apparently means that the matter of near kindred is
overborne in importance by the consideration of her loneliness and of
the necessity for continuing their race. The verse agrees throughout
with RV. x. 10. 11. The comm. renders -m┼лt─Б in c by m┼лrchit─Б.

Griffith

Is he a brother when no help is left her? Is she a sister when Destruction cometh? Forced by my love these many words I utter. Come near, and hold me in thy close embraces,

Whitney
Translation
  1. I am not thy protector here, O Yam─л; I may not mingle my body with
    thy body; with another than me do thou prepare enjoyments; thy brother
    wants not that, O fortunate one.
Notes

All our mss. save Op.K. accent y├бmi in a; SPP. reports only one of
his as doing so. RV. x. 10. 12 is in our text expanded into two verses,
its second half being our c, d, without variant. The comm. reads
n┼лnam for tan┼лm in b; he explains n─Бth├бm in a by
abhimat─Бrthasamp─Бdakas.

Griffith

I am no help for thee, no refuge, Yami, I will not clasp and press thee to my bosom. This is abhorrent to my mind and spirit–a brother on the couch beside a sister.

резрек рди рд╡рд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Verily, I may not mingle my body with thy body; they call him wicked
    (p─Бp├б) who should approach his sister. That is not consonant (?
    asaс╣Бy├бt) with my mind [and] heart, that I, a brother, should lie in
    a sister’s bed (┼Ы├бyana).
Notes

The first half-verse тМКcf. vs. 13тМЛ is RV. x. 10. 12 a, b, which
latter, however, reads in a te tanv─Б╠А tanv├ас╣Б s├бm. All the mss.
leave ┼Ыay─лya at the end unaccented, and both editions read
accordingly; we ought in ours to have made the necessary emendation to
┼Ы├бy─лya. The mss. vary in c between ├бsaс╣Бyat, asaс╣Бy├бt, ├бsaс╣Бy├бt,
and asaс╣Бyat; SPP. gives in his text ├бsaс╣Бyat, which is better than
our asaс╣Бy├бt; the pada-text divides asamре░yat. The comm. reads
instead asuс╣Б yat, and supplies a verb, apaharet, to govern asum.

Griffith

I will not fold mine arms about thy body: they call it sin when one comes near a sister. Not me–prepare thy pleasure with another. Thy brother seeks not this from thee, O fair one.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A weakling (? bat├б), alas, art thou, O Yama; we have not found
    mind and heart thine; verily, another woman shall embrace thee, as a
    girth a harnessed [horse], as a twining plant (l├нbuj─Б) a tree.
Notes

RV. x. 10. 13 varies from this only by reading (as also our Bp.) in
d с╣гvaj─Бte. The translation given of kakс╣гy├и тАЩva yukt├бm agrees
with the comm. (also the comm. to RV.), which renders yuktam by
svasambaddham a┼Ыvam. P─Бda b evidently alludes to 14 c, where
Yama talks of his mind and heart. If bat├бs is a genuine word (the
metrical disarray intimates corruption), it looks like being the noun of
which the common exclamation bata is by origin the vocative. The RV.
Anukr. takes no notice of the defective meter; ours requires the verse
to be read as only 40 syllables, which is possible (10 + 9: 10 + 11 =
40); тМКc and d are good triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бdas and b has a
triс╣гс╣нubh cadenceтМЛ.

Griffith

Alas; thou art indeed a weakling Yama. We find in thee no trace o f heart or spirit. As round a tree the woodbine clings, another will cling about thee girt as with a girdle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Another man, truly, O Yam─л, another man shall embrace thee, as a
    twining plant a tree; either do thou seek his mind or he thine; then
    make for thyself very excellent concord (samv├нd).
Notes

RV. x. 10. 14 has for a the much better version any├бm ┼л с╣г├║ tv├бс╣Б
yamy any├б u tv─Б╠Бm, and in b again с╣гvaj─Бte. Our D., and a single
ms. of SPP’s (with the comm.), also have anyam тМКat the beginningтМЛ, and
SPP. accordingly admits any├бm into his text, in spite of the absence
of tv├бm. But the comment on the Pr─Бt. three times (under ii. 97; iii.
4; iv. 98) reads anya ┼л с╣гu, and it cannot well be questioned that this
is the true text of our AV. Our P.M.E. accent again y├бmi. The Anukr.
takes no notice of the lacking syllable in a; тМКperhaps it balances
c against aтМЛ.

Griffith

Embrace another, Yami. Let some other, even as the woodbine rings a tree, enfold thee. Win thou his heart and let him win thy fancy; so make with him a bond of blest alliance.

Translation
  1. Three meters the poets extended (? vi-yat)тАФthe many-formed one,
    the admirable, the all-beholding; waters, winds, herbsтАФthese are set
    (─Б╠Бrpita) in one being (bh├║vana).
Notes

The verse is extremely obscure, in meaning and in connection. The mss.
vary much as regards the accent of purur┼лpam; two of ours (O.D.) and
several of SPP’s accent -r┼л╠Бp-, which, as it is found in other texts,
the latter has very properly admitted in his edition. The comm. renders
v├н yetire by yatnaс╣Б kс╣Ыtavantaс╕е. The Anukr. takes no notice of the
irregularity of the meter. тМКConcerning this prakс╣гipta-verse,
“glossenartige Parallelstelle,” see Weber, Sb. 1895, p. 819 note, and
p. 828.тМЛ

Griffith

Three hymns the Sages have disposed in order, the many-formed, the fair, the all-beholding. These in one single world are placed and settled–the growing plants, the breezes, and the waters.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The bull yieldeth (duh) milks for the bull with the milking of the
    sky (d├нv), he the unharmable son (? yahv├б) of Aditi; everything
    knoweth he, like Varuс╣Зa, by thought (dh─л╠Б); he, sharing the sacrifice
    (yaj├▒├нya), sacrificeth to the seasons that share the sacrifice.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 11. 1, whose only variant is yajatu for -ti in
d. The comm. explains vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б as Agni, and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зe as the sacrificer,
d├│has─Б as = dohanas─Бdhanena yaj├▒─Бdin─Б, yahv├бs as mah─Бn and
qualifying vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б together with ├бd─Бbhyas, while ├бdites means
“indivisible” and qualifies div├бs, which is ablative: the general
sense being that the god procures rain for his worshiper. His
understanding of c agrees with the translation given above. Compare
Pischel’s version of the verse and general explanation of the RV. hymn
in Ved. Stud. i. 183 ff.; his exposition is excessively ingenious and
extremely unsatisfactory.

Griffith

The Bull hath yielded for the Bull the milk of heaven: inviolable is the Son of Aditi. According to his wisdom Varuna knoweth all: he halloweth, the holy, times for sacrifice.

Translation
  1. Prateth the Gandharv─л and watery woman; in the noise of the noisy
    one (nad├б) let [her] protect our mind; let Aditi set us in the midst
    of what is desired (? iс╣гс╣н├б); our oldest brother shall first speak out.

the first half-verse appears to be defective; but it certainly

Griffith

Gandharvi spake. May she, the Lady of the Flood amid the river’s roaring leave my heart untouched. May Aditi accomplish all that we desire, and may our eldest Brother tell us this as chief.

Translation
  1. Then that mighty (vibh┼л╠Б) conspicuous drop did the bird, the lively
    falcon, bring at the sacrifice; if the Aryan tribes (v├н┼Ы) choose the
    wondrous one, Agni, [as] h├│tс╣Ы, then prayer (dh─л╠Б) was born.
Notes

RV. x. 11. 4 differs only by reading iс╣гit├бs in b. The comm. makes
a couple of references, to TB. iii. 2. 1┬╣ and TS. vi. 1. 6┬╣, where the
legends of the bringing of soma from heaven by the falcon are given.
Pr─Бt. iii. 25 notes the short final of ├бdha in a and d.

Griffith

And the fleet Falcon brought for sacrifice from afar this flowing. drop most excellent and passing wise, Then when the Aryan tribes chose as invoking Priest Agni the wonder-worker, and the hymn rose up.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ever art thou pleasant (raс╣Зv├б), as pastures to him that enjoys
    (puс╣г) them, being, O Agni, well sacrificed to with the offerings of
    man (m├бnus); or when, active, praiseworthy, having won the strength
    (v─Б╠Бja) of the inspired one (v├нpra), thou approachest with very many.
Notes

RV. x. 11. 5 differs only by reading ukthy├аm at end of c. The
construction and meaning of the second half-verse are difficult and
obscure. The comm. explains ┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бnas by ┼Ыaс╣Еsan yajam─Бnam pra┼Ыaс╣Еsan
(similarly the comm. to RV.); and bh┼лribhis as “accompanied by many
desires or else by many gods” (RV. comm. only the latter).

Griffith

Still art thou kind to him who feeds thee as with grass, and. skilled in sacrifice offers thee holy gifts. When thou having received the sage’s strengthening food with lauds, after long toil comest with many more.

реирей рдЙрджреАрд░рдп рдкрд┐рддрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рд░ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Send thou up the (two) fathers, [as] a lover, unto enjoyment
    (bh├бga). The welcome one (haryat├б) desires to sacrifice; he sends
    from the heart; the bearer (v├бhni) speaks out; the merry one (?
    makh├б) does a good work; the Asura shows might (taviс╣гy); he trembles
    with purpose (? mat─л╠Б).
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 11. 6, without variant. It is extremely obscure, and
the general sense, as well as the meaning of several words, is in a high
degree doubtful; the translation given is no more than mechanical. тМКCf.
Weber, p. 829.тМЛ The ’two fathers’ (parents) are declared by the comm.,
probably rightly, to be heaven and earth; j─Бras is explained as
─Бdityas, and ─Б as = iva. Or, alternatively, j─Бras is “praiser,”
coming from jar─Б “praise,” and to a is to be supplied hvayati.
The iс╣гyati is made = icchati; vahni is Agni; makhas is
makhas─Бdhano maс╣Еhan─лyo v─Б; taviс╣гyate is vardhiс╣гyate. All this is
of interest only as showing that no help is to be obtained from the
native exegetes.

Griffith

Urge thou thy Parents, as a lover, to delight: the lovely One desires and craves it from his heart. As Priest he calls aloud, as Warrior shows his skill, as Asura tries his strength, and with the hymn is stirred.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whatever mortal hath seen thy favor, O Agni, son of power, he is
    renowned exceedingly; acquiring (dh─Б) food (├нс╣г), borne by horses,
    he, lightful, vigorous, passes (? ─Б-bh┼лс╣г) the days (d├нv).
Notes

RV. x. 11. 7 reads in a ├бkс╣гat, of which our ├бkhyat is doubtless
only a corruption. Our Bp. and one of SPP’s authorities have akс╣гat.
The comm. renders ─Б bh┼лс╣гati by ─Бbhavati; тМКhe adds alternatively:
bh┼лс╣гati = bubh┼лс╣гati, dyum─Бn…bhavitum icchatiтМЛ. In b he reads
abhi instead of ati.

Griffith

Far famed is he, the mortal man, O Agni thou Son of strength, who hath obtained thy favour. He, gathering power, borne onward by his horses, makes his, days lovely in his might and splendour.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Hear us, O Agni, in thy seat, thy station; harness the speedy
    chariot of the immortal (amс╣Ы╠Бta); bring to us the two firmaments
    (r├│das─л), parents of the gods; be thou of the gods never (m─Б╠Бkis)
    away; mayest thou be here.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 11. 9 (and 12. 9), without variant. The comm.
comfortably supplies saс╣Бghe in d to govern the genitive dev─Бn─Бm.
Then, as alternative explanation, he understands bh┼лs and sy─Бs as
third persons, and m─Б╠Бkis as “no one.”

Griffith

Hear us, O Agni, in the great assembly: harness thy rapid car,. the car of Amrit. Bring Heaven and Earth, the Deities’ Parents, hither: stay with us here, nor from the Gods be absent.

Whitney
Translation
  1. That, O Agni, this meeting may take place (bh┼л), divine, among the
    gods, worshipful, thou reverend one, and that thou mayest share out
    treasures, O self-ruling one, do thou enjoy here our portion filled with
    good things.
Notes

The verse is, without variant, RV. x. 11. 8 (also found in MS. iv. 14.
15).

Griffith

When, holy Agni, the divine assembly, the holy synod mid the Gods, is gathered, And when thou, godlike One, dealest forth treasures vouchsafe us too our portion of the riches.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Agni hath looked after the apex of the dawns, after the days, [he]
    first, J─Бtavedas; a sun, after the dawns, after the rays; after

Notes
Griffith

Agni hath looked upon the van of Mornings, and on the days. the earliest Jatavedas. After the Dawns, after their rays of brightness, Surya hath enter- ed into earth and heaven.

Agni hath looked against the van of Mornings, against the days- the earliest Jatavedas; In many a place against the beams of Surya, against the heavens and earth hath he extended.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A god, encompassing the gods with right, carry thou first our
    offering, understanding [it]; smoke-bannered by the fuel,
    light-beaming, a pleasant, constant h├│tс╣Ы, skilled sacrificer with
    speech.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 12. 2, without variant. The majority of SPP’s mss.,
with one of ours (Op.), read bh─Б╠Бrc─лko in c. Neither our Anukr. nor
that of the RV. notes the deficiency of a syllable in a.

Griffith

As God comprising Gods by Law eternal, bear, as the chief who knoweth, our oblation, Smoke-bannered with the fuel, radiant, joyous, better to praise and worship, Priest for ever.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I praise (arc) your (du.) work unto increase, ye ghee-surfaced
    ones; O heaven-and-earth, hear me, ye two firmaments (r├│das─л); when
    days, O gods, went to the other life (├бsun─лti), let the two parents
    (pit├бr─Б) sharpen us here with honey.
Notes

The rendering is only mechanical, the obscurity of the verse being
unresolved. It is RV. x. 12. 4, which, however, reads for c ├бh─Б y├бd
dy─Б╠Бv├│ тАШsun─лtim ├бyan. Our mss. and the authorities of SPP. vary in c
between dev─Б╠Бs, d├йv─Бs, and dev─Бs; SPP. reads dev─Б╠Бs, with тМКat
leastтМЛ two of his; our d├йv─Бs is not defensible; the translation
implies dev─Бs. The comm. makes the word the subject of ─Б╠Бyan, taking
├бh─Б (p. ├бh─Б) as for ahaс╕еsu; he explains dev─Бs by stot─Бras or
с╣Ыtvijas. Our Bp. is the only pada-ms. that reads (with the RV.
pada) ├бpaс╕е in a; the others have ─Б╠Бpaс╕е; but, as the comm. gives
the former, SPP. adopts it in his text. A majority of SPP’s mss. accent
ghс╣Ыt├бsn┼л, but only one of ours (O.) does so.

Griffith

I praise your work .that ye may make me prosper: hear, Heaven and Earth, twain worlds that drop with fatness! While days and Gods go to the world of spirits, have let the Parents with sweet mead refresh us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If the god’s immortality (amс╣Ы╠Бta) is easy to appropriate for the
    cow, thence those who are born maintain themselves on the broad
    [earth]; all the gods go after that sacrificial formula of thine, when
    the hind yields (duh) the ghee, heavenly liquor (v─Б╠Бr).
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 12. 3, without variant. It is all extremely obscure,
especially the first p─Бda, which admits of being rendered in
half-a-dozen different ways; the translation given is purely tentative.
The comm. gives little help. The pada-text does not divide or
otherwise change sv─Б╠Бvс╣Ыk, which indicates that its makers did not see
in the word the formation su-─Б-vс╣Ыj, which is plausibly seen in it by
western scholars and by our comm. The latter takes urv─л╠Б (p. urv─л╠Б
├нti) as dual, but in the Pr─Бt. it is quoted by the comment (to i. 74)
as example of a locative in ─л, which it doubtless is. Our comm.
derives y├бjus first from root yuj and makes it = karman; dev─Бs
is again, as above (vs. 31), stot─Бras, с╣Ыtvijas. тМКWith the expression
divy├бс╣Б v─Б╠Бс╕е, applied to ghee, compare the expression at x. 4. 3, v─Б╠Бr
ugr├бm, applied to snake-venom, which may well be called a ’terrible
fluid’: but see note to x. 4. 3.тМЛ

Griffith

When the Cow’s nectar wins the God completely, men here below are heaven’s and earth’s sustainers All the Gods come to this thy heavenly Yajus which from the motley Pair milked oil and water

Whitney
Translation
  1. Why forsooth hath the king seized (grah) us? what have we done in
    transgression of (├бti) his ordinance (vrat├б)? who discerns [it]?
    for even Mitra, swerving the gods, like a song of praise (┼Ыl├│ka), is
    the might also of them that go.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 12. 5, without variant. The second half-verse,
especially the last p─Бda, is bafflingly obscure. The accent of ├бsti,
as well as the absence of other construction for mitr├бs, strongly
indicates that the whole of the second half-verse forms one sentence; in
which case v─Б╠Бjas is perhaps most probably a corruption. The comm.
understands r─Б╠Бj─Б in a as Yama, and jagс╣Ыhe as signifying his
“acceptance” of offeringsтАФwhich is very ill guessed; doubtless it is
Varuс╣Зa (so Ludwig; the RV. comm. makes it Agni). He then renders
juhur─Бс╣З├бs most absurdly by ─Бhvayan, тМКsaying that “the root hvс╣Ы
‘crook’ is here used in the sense of root h┼л ‘call’"тМЛ. He reads in
d (as do some of the mss., including our O.Op.R.) y─Бt─Бn, as accus.
of the pple y─Бta, qualifying dev─Бn understood, rendering dev─Бn
abhigacchato no тАШsm─Бn rakс╣гitum! and so on. The version of the line
given above is of course mechanical only.

Griffith

Hath the King seized us? How have we offended against his holy Ordinance? Who knoweth? For even Mitra mid the Gods is angry. There are both song and wealth for those who come not.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХрд┐рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН) рдХреНрдпреЛрдВ [рдХрд┐рд╕ рдХрд░реНрдордлрд▓ рд╕реЗ] (рдирдГ) рд╣рдореЗрдВ (рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ [рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] рдиреЗ (рдЬрдЧреГрд╣реЗ) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ [рд╕реБрдЦ рджрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ], (рдХрддреН) рдХрдм (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЗ (рд╡реНрд░рддрдореН) рдирд┐рдпрдо рдХреЛ (рдЕрддрд┐ рдЪрдХреГрдо)рд╣рдордиреЗ рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рдЩреНрдШрди рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ [рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд╕реЗ рдХреНрд▓реЗрд╢ рдкрд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ], (рдХрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ [рдЗрд╕ рдХреЛ] (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рд╡реЗрдж) рдЬрд╛рдирддрд╛ рд╣реИред (рд╣рд┐) рдХреНрдпреЛрдВрдХрд┐ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ) рд╕рдмрдХрд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рд╣реА (рд╕реНрдо) рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдп (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдЙрдиреНрдорддреНрддреЛ рдХреЛ (рдЬреБрд╣реБрд░рд╛рдгрдГ) рдорд░реЛрдбрд╝ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдФрд░ (рдпрд╛рддрд╛рдореН) рдЧрддрд┐рд╢реАрд▓реЛрдВ [рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ] рдХрд╛ (рдЕрдкрд┐) рд╣реА (рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрдГ рди) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╡рд╛рдЬрдГ) рдмрд▓ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐) рд╣реИ реерейрейрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Hard to reverence (? durm├бntu) here is the name of the immortal,
    that she of like sign should become of diverse form; whoso shall
    reverence Yama with proper reverence (? sum├бntu), him, O Agni, exalted
    one, do thou protect, unremitting.
Notes

This verse is found also as RV. x. 12. 6, without variant, but the RV.
comm. passes it without notice, as if recognizing it as not genuine. It
is very strange to find repeated here as b vs. 2 b, above, as
the connection this time does not explain the feminine words in it. The
comm. first explains (like Grassmann) the p─Бda as quoted from the other
verse; but goes on to add other interpretations. He defines durm├бntu
by durmananaс╣Б durvacam.

Griffith

‘Tis hard to understand the Immortal’s nature, where she who is akin becomes a stranger. Guard ceaselessly, great Agni, him who ponders Yama’s name easy to be comprehended.

Translation
  1. In whom the gods revel at the council, maintain themselves in
    Vivasvant’s seatтАФthey placed light in the sun, rays in the moon: the
    two, unfailing, wait upon (pari-car) the brightness (dyotan├н).
Notes

The verse is x. 12. 7, without variant. The comm. separates y├бsmin
from vid├бthe, supplying agn─Бu for the former to qualify (the RV.
comm. does the same); perhaps rather manmani is to be inferred from
the following verse. тМКW. suggests by a note to his ms. as an alternative
for a, ‘In what council the gods revel.’тМЛ Our comm. also explains,
in d, dyotan├нm by dyotam─Бnam agnim, and it reads ajasram,
understanding it adverbially; akt┼лn in c is either ra┼Ыm─лn or
r─Бtr─лs. тМКThis vs. and the next are discussed by Foy, KZ. xxxiv. 228.тМЛ

Griffith

They in the synod where the Gods rejoice them, where they are seated in Vivasvan’s dwelling, Have given the Moon his beams, the Sun his splendour: the two unweariedly maintain their brightness.

The counsel which the Gods meet to consider, their secret plan, of that we have no knowledge. There let God Savitar, Aditi, and Mitra proclaim to Varuna that we are sinless.

Translation
  1. O companions, we would supplicate (─Б-┼Ыas) worship (br├бhman) for
    Indra, possessor of the thunderbolt, to praise, indeed, the most manly,
    the daring.
Notes

The verse is RV. viii. 24. 1 (also SV. i. 390), which reads in a
┼Ыiс╣г─Бmahi (SV. -he), and inserts in c vas after ┼л с╣г├║, as
required by the meter. The comm’s text (but not his exposition) also has
the vas. Our Anukr. takes no notice of the lack of a syllable in the
p─Бda. The comm. explains ─Б╠Б ┼Ыiс╣г─Бmahe by ─Б┼Ы─Бsmahe, and supplies
kartum; he renders stuс╣г├й by either st─Бumi or stotum. The
particles ┼л с╣г├║ are included in the prescriptions of Pr─Бt. ii. 97; iii.
4; iv. 98. тМКWeber, Sb. 1895, p. 819 n., can assign no reason why vss.
37-38 should appear here.тМЛ

Griffith

Companions, let us learn a prayer to Indra whom the thunder arms, To glorify your bold and most heroic Friend.

Translation
  1. For thou art famed for might (┼Ы├бvas), for Vritra-slaying, a
    Vritra-slayer; thou out-bestowest the bounteous with thy bounties, O
    hero.
Notes

The verse is RV. viii. 24. 2, and without variant, if, with SPP., we
read ┼Ыrut├бs at end of a. Our text has ┼Ыrit├бs, with a part of the
mss.; they vary between ┼Ыrut├бs (our O.Op.D.R., and half of SPP’s;
also the comm.), ┼Ыrit├бs (our P.M.T., and two of SPP’s), and ┼Ыс╣Ыt├бs
(our Bp.Bs.E.I.K.Kp., and three or four of SPP’s authorities)тАФwhich last
is doubtless only a careless variant of ┼Ыrit├бs. The translation given
above implies ┼Ыrut├бs. The comm. perhaps reads in b vс╣Ыtrahatye
тАЩva.

Griffith

For thou by slaying Vritra art the Vritra-slayer, famed for might. Thou, Hero, in rich gifts surpassest wealthy chiefs.

Translation
  1. Thou goest over the earth as a steg├б over the ground; let winds
    blow here on the great earth (bh┼л╠Бmi) for us; Mitra for us there
    (├бtra), Varuс╣Зa, being joined, hath let loose heat (┼Ы├│ka), as fire
    does in the forest.

bh┼л╠Бma; in c, y├бtra (for no ├бtra) and ajy├бm─Бnas (for yuj-);
in d, тАШgn├нr v-. Part of the AV. mss. also have тАШgn├нr v- (our
O.R., and nearly half of SPP’s), which accordingly might well be adopted
in the text; but SPP., like our edition, reads agn├нr v-. One or two of
our mss. (Op.R.s.m.) read in d asс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa (vy├аs-), and so do a
minority of SPP’s; and the latter gives in his saс╣Бhit─Б-text
vy├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa, but (apparently by an oversight) in his pada-text v├н:
asс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa; one sees no reason at all for the accentuation of the verb тМКthe
AV. text, with its ├бtraтМЛ.* Our text is plainly an unintelligent
corruption of an unintelligible verse. The RV. comm. guesses
ra┼Ыmisaс╣Бgh─Бty ─Бdityaс╕е to be the meaning of the тМКvery rareтМЛ steg├б,
but only on the ground of a worthless etymology. Our comm. is defective
here, but the lacuna is filled up by the editor, who makes it signify “a

vy├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa by n─Б┼Ыayatu! The с╣Б of pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Б is тМКalmost or quite

*тМКThe RV. reads vy ├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa, and has the difficult pada-reading v├н:
├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa: here the RV’s accentuation of ├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa is accounted for by the
RV’s y├бtra; and the accent of v├н is to be put with the remarkable
cases (some thirty) mentioned by W., Gram. ┬з 1084 a, whether we regard
it as a blunder helped by the wavering tradition as to ├бtra, y├бtra, or
not. (Cf. what is said about “blend-readings” under xiv. 2. 18 and, just
below, under xviii. 1. 42.) Whitney’s Bp. follows the RV. in giving v├н:
├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa and his Bs. has vy├бsс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa; cf. the v├н: ├бdadhus of xix. 6. 5

Griffith

O’er the broad land thou goest like a Stega: here on vast earth let breezes blow upon us, Here hath our dear Friend Varuna, united, like Agni in the wood, shot forth his splendour.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Praise thou the famed sitter on the hollow of men (j├бna), the
    terrible king, formidable assailant (? upahatn├║); being praised, O
    Rudra, be gracious to the singer; let thine army (? s├йnya) lay low
    (ni-vap) another than us.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. ii. 33. 11 (also found in TS. iv. 5. 10┬│,
without variant from RV.), which reads in a-b -s├бdaс╣Б y├║v─Бnam mс╣Ыg├бс╣Б
n├б bh-, and, for d, тАШny├бс╣Б te asm├бn n├н vapantu s├йn─Бс╕е. The
substitution in our text of s├йnyam for s├йn─Бs at the end throws into
confusion sense and construction. The comm. first takes it as = sen─Бs,
and then as accus. qualifying any├бm and signifying tava sen─Бrham, in
the latter case supplying sen─Бs as subject of the verb. Gartas├бdam
he takes first in the Nirukta sense of ┼Ыma┼Ы─Бnasaс╣Бcaya, and then in its
“ordinary” (prasiddha) meaning, adding tasy─Б тАЩraс╣Зye saс╣Бc─Бr─Бd
gartasadanaс╣Б yujyate. The K─Бu┼Ы. (85. 19) uses the verse in connection
with the digging of a hollow (garta) in the middle of the measured
space at the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a, and the scattering into it of a number of
heterogeneous substances. Our comm., by some rare and strange
oversight, makes no mention of this viniyoga, and so does not take it
into account in the explanation of the verse. Apparently it is only the
occurrence of gartasad in the verse that suggests the use; of real
applicability to the situation there is none.

Griffith

Sing praise to him the chariot-borne, the famous, Sovran of men, the dread and strong destroyer. O Rudra, praised be gracious to the singer; let thy darts spare us and smite down another.

Whitney
Translation
  1. On Sarasvat─л do the pious call; on Sarasvat─л , while the sacrifice
    is being extended; on Sarasvat─л do the well-doers call: may Sarasvat─л
    give what is desirable to the worshiper (d─Б┼Ыv─Б╠Бс╣Еs).
Notes

RV. x. 17. 7 is the same verse, but makes better meter by having
ahvayanta for havante in c; and the comm. agrees with it. Verses
41-43, with others to Sarasvat─л (vii. 68. 1-2; also xviii. 3. 25), are
used by K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 39) in the pitс╣Ыmedha ceremony, accompanying
offerings to Sarasvat─л. тМКAnd they recur below, as noted under vs. 43.тМЛ
The Anukr. takes no notice of the deficiency of a syllable in 41 c,
and 42 a, nor of the excess of two syllables in 43 a.

Griffith

The pious call Sarasvati, they worship Sarasvati while sacrifice proceedeth. The virtuous call Sarasvati to hear them. Sarasvati send bliss to him who giveth!

  1. On Sarasvat─л do the Fathers call, arriving at the sacrifice on the

Here again the RV. version (x. 17. 9 a, b, 8 c, d) makes the
meter good by inserting тМКor rather (cf. vs. 59), by not omittingтМЛ y─Б╠Бm
in a before pit├бras (and hence accenting h├бvante*); it also
accents dakс╣гiс╣З─Б╠Б in b, as other texts do; two of our mss.
(O.s.m.Op.) do the same, with the majority of SPP’s, whence the latter
adopts dakс╣гiс╣З─Б╠Б in his edition; it is undoubtedly the correct reading
тМКas is explicitly stated also by the comm. to xix. 13. 9, page 325┬▓┬╣тМЛ.
RV. also avoids the change of subject in the second line by reading
m─Бdayasva in c. *тМКIt is interesting to note that SPP’s C^(P)
accents h├бvante, as if the missing y─Б╠Бm were not missing: cf. my note
about “blend-readings” under xiv. 2. 18, and the end of my note under
xviii. 1. 39; also note to 4. 57.тМЛ

Griffith

Sarasvati is called on by the Fathers who come right forward to our solemn worship. Seated upon this sacred grass rejoice you. Give thou us strengthening food that brings no sickness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Sarasvat─л, that wentest in company (sar├бtham) with the songs
    (ukth├б), with the svadh─Б╠Бs, O goddess, reveling with the Fathers,
    assign thou to the sacrificer here a portion of refreshment (├нс╕Н) of
    thousandfold value, abundance of wealth.
Notes

Here, once more, the AV. disturbs the meter by the intrusion into a
of ukth─Б├нs, which is wanting in the RV. version (x. 17. 8 a, b, 9
c, d). тМКRV. reads y├бjam─Бneс╣гu in d.тМЛ The three Sarasvat─л verses
are repeated below as xviii. 4. 45-47. The comm. gives annasya as
equivalent of iс╕Н├бs.

Griffith

Sarasvati, who comest with the Fathers, joying in hymns, O Goddess, and oblations, Give plenteous wealth to this the sacrificer, a portion, worth a thousand, of refreshment.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the lower, let the higher, let the midmost Fathers, the
    soma-drinking (? somy├б), go up; they who went to life (├бsu),
    unharmed (avс╣Ыk├б), right-knowingтАФlet those Fathers aid us at our calls.
Notes

The verse is found, without variant, as RV. x. 15. 1, VS. xix. 49, and
in TS. ii. 6. 12┬│, MS. iv. 10. 6. It is used twice by K─Бu┼Ы. in the
funeral book: once (80. 43) at the piling of the funeral pile, and once
(87. 14), in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a, at the digging of a pit for receiving
certain offerings. Verses 44-46 appear together (87. 29) in the latter
ceremony with the bringing in of certain water-pots тМКi.e. the pouring in
(of their contents)?тМЛ. In V─Бit. (30. 14), vss. 44 and 45, with 51, and
3. 44, 45, are prescribed to be repeated after the pouring of sur─Б
into a perforated vessel, in the s─Бutr─Бmaс╣З─л ceremony; and again, vss.
44-46 accompany (37. 23) the binding of a victim to the sacrificial post
in the puruс╣гamedha.

Griffith

May they ascend, the lowest, highest, midmost, the Fathers, who deserve a share of Soma. May they who have attained to life, the Fathers, righteous and gentle, aid us when we call them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I have won hither (─Б-vid) the beneficent Fathers, both the
    grandson and the wide-striding of Vishс╣Зu; they who, sitting on the
    barh├нs, partake of the pressed drink with svadh─Б╠БтАФthey come
    especially hither.
Notes

The verse is, without variant, RV. x. 15. 3, VS. xix. 56, and found in
TS. ii. 6. 12┬│ and MS. iv. 10. 6 (MS. puts y├й after svadh├бy─Б in
c). Our comm. is uncertain from which root vid to make avitsi,
and casts no light on the obscure second p─Бda; he renders ─Бgamiс╣гс╣нh─Бs
either by ─Бgamaya or ─Бgacchantu. The abbreviated form barhiс╣г├бdas
(p. barhiре░s├бdaс╕е) is one of those quoted by the Pr─Бt. comment as aimed
at by rules ii. 59; iv. 100. For the use of the verse by K─Бu┼Ы. and
V─Бit., see under vs. 44.

Griffith

I have attained the gracious-minded Fathers, I have gained son and progeny from Vishnu. They who enjoy pressed juices with oblation, seated on sacred grass, come oftenest hither.

рекрем рдЗрджрдВ рдкрд┐рддреГрднреНрдпреЛрдирдореЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Be this homage today to the Fathers, who went first, who went after,
    who are seated in the space (r├бjas) of earth, or who are now in
    regions (d├н┼Ы) having good abodes (suvс╣Ыj├бna).
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 15. 2, which, however, reads in b ├║par─Бsas,
and in d vikс╣г├║; and with it in both respects read the
corresponding verses in TS. ii. 6. 12тБ┤ and MS. iv. 10. 6; also VS. xix.
68 (but this, with our E., has n├бmo тАШstu in a). Ppp. also gives
the verse in book ii., reading in b ye par─Бsaс╣г pareyuс╕е, and in
d suvс╣Ыjin─Бsu vikс╣гu. Some of our mss. (P.M.I.R.T.), and one of
SPP’s, agree with RV. in reading ├║par─Бsas; the comm. divides u
par─Бsas; and our E. has vikс╣г├║, while P.M. give divikс╣г├║, and I.
prikс╣г├║. For the use of the verse in K─Бu┼Ы. and V─Бit. with vss. 44-45,
see under 44; it also (or else, more probably, 4. 51: see under that
verse) is prescribed alone (80. 51) to accompany the scattering of
darbha-grass in preparing the funeral pile.

Griffith

Now be this homage offered to the Fathers, to those who passed of old and those who followed, Those who have rested in the earthly region and those who dwell among the happy races.

Griffith

Matali prospers there with Kavyas, Yama with Angiras’ sons, Brihaspati with singers. Exalters of the Gods, by Gods exalted, aid us those Fathers in our invocations?

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛рддрд▓реА) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рдпрдордГ) рд╕рдВрдпрдореА рдФрд░ (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐ [рдмрдбрд╝реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖] (рдХрд╡реНрдпреИрдГ) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╣рд┐рддрдХрд╛рд░реА (рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреА рдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рдЛрдХреНрд╡рднрд┐рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝рд╛рдИрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╛рдирдГ) рдмрдврд╝рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдпрд╛рдиреН) рдЬрд┐рди [рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ] рдХреЛ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдиреЗ (рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзреБрдГ) рдмрдврд╝рд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдпреЗ) рдЬрд┐рди [рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ]рдиреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ [рдмрдврд╝рд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ], (рддреЗ) рд╡реЗ (рдкрд┐рддрд░рдГ) рдкрд┐рддрд░ [рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ]рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдореЗрдВ (рд╣рд╡реЗрд╖реБ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрд╡рдиреНрддреБ) рдмрдЪрд╛рд╡реЗрдВ реерекренрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Sweet verily is this [s├│ma], and full of honey is this; strong
    (t─лvr├б) verily is this, and full of sap is this; and no one soever
    overpowers in conflicts (─Бhav├б) Indra, having now drunk of it.
Notes

The verse is RV. vi. 47. 1, without real variant; its applicability in
the funeral book is not apparent, and neither K─Бu┼Ы. nor V─Бit. uses it.
Part of our mss. (O.R.K.), with nearly all SPP’s, combine at the
beginning sv─Бd├║с╣г k-, which RV. also has; and SPP., with good reason,
adopts this in his text.

Griffith

Yes, this is good to taste and full of sweetness, verily it is strong and rich in flavour. No one may conquer Indra in the battle when he hath drunken of the draught we offer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Him that went away to the advances called great, spying out the road
    for many, Vivasvant’s son, gatherer of people, king Yama, honor
    (sapary) ye with oblation.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 14. 1, which, however, reads ├бnu for ├нti at end
of a, and duvasya for saparyata in d. A verse in MS. iv. 14.
16 has the RV. version throughout. TA. (in vi. 1. 1) gives at the end
the genuine variant duvasyata, but also in a and b the
incredible blunders pare yuv─Б╠Бс╣Еsam and anapaspa┼Ы─Бn├бm; тМКso even the
Poona ed., p. 405тМЛ. With the first half-verse is to be compared our vi.
28. 3 a, b. The ├нti of our version, at end of a, seems a
worthless corruption (SPP. thinks it certainly “a mistake for ├бti”;
but that is not very plausible, though our I., doubtless by an
accidental slip, has ├бti, and P.M. have ata); the comm. reads anu,
with the other texts. тМКWith this vs. and the next, cf. 3. 13 below: the
second half of 3. 13 is identical with the second half of this vs.тМЛ In
K─Б├║┼Ы. (81. 34), recital of the verse accompanies offerings to Yama at
the lighting of the funeral pile. Metrically, it is svar─Бj (12 + 11:
11 + 12 = 46) rather than bhurij. тМКCaland, Todtengebr├дuche, p. 65,
observes that “K─Бu┼Ы. 81. 34-36 [meaning 34-37] form one single whole.”
They indicate the eleven verses (translated by C, p. 64) that are to be
used to accompany the eleven oblations to Yama (y─Бm─Бn hom─Бn), offered
in the pitс╣Ыmedha, after the lighting of the fire. The vss. are: xviii.

  1. 49, 50, for the first two oblations; xviii. 1. 58, 59, 60, 61 (the
    last vs. of the hymn) and xviii. 2. 1, 2, 3, for the next seven; and
    xviii. 3. 13 and 2. 49, for the last two: in all, eleven, ity ek─Бda┼Ыa.
    Whereupon follow the oblations to Sarasvat─л.тАФIt should be noted that the
    group 1. 58 to 2. 3 (K─Бu┼Ы.: iti saс╣Бhit─Бс╕е sapta) disregards the
    existing division of the book into anuv─Бka-hymns.тМЛ
Griffith

Honour the King with your oblations, Yama, Vivasvan’s son, who gathers men together. Even him who travelled o’er the mighty rivers, who searches out and shows the path to many.

релреж рдпрдореЛ рдиреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Yama first found for us a track (g─Бt├║); that is not a pasture to
    be borne away; where our former Fathers went forth, there (en─Б╠Б) [go]
    those born [of them], along their own roads.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 14. 2) reads parey├║s at end of c,
and MS. (in iv. 14. 16) agrees with it. The comm. has yena instead of
en─Б in d. The verse (with vs. 51?) is used by K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 35) next
after the preceding one, in the same ceremony.

Griffith

Yama first found for us the road to travel: this pasture never can be taken from us. Men born on earth tread their own paths that lead them whither our ancient Fathers have departed.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ye barh├нs-seated Fathers, hitherward with aid! these offerings
    have we made for you; enjoy [them]! do ye come with most wealful aid;
    then assign to us weal [and] profit, free from evil.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 15. 4) has ├бth─Б at beginning of d.
VS. (xix. 55) agrees throughout with RV.; TS. (in ii. 6. 12┬▓) spoils the
meter of d by changing nas to asm├бbhyam; MS. (in iv. 10. 6) has
at the end dadh─Бtana; тМКso has W’s Op.тМЛ. The comm. also reads atha.
The verse is used by K─Бu┼Ы. (87. 27), along with 3. 44-46 and 4. 68, to
accompany the untying and strewing of the barhis in the
piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a. In V─Бit. 30. 14, it appears with 1. 44, 45 etc. (see
under 1. 44); and again (9. 8), in the c─Бturm─Бsya sacrifice,
accompanying (with 3. 44, 45 and 4. 71) a libation to Soma and the
Fathers.

Griffith

Fathers who sit on sacred grass, come, help us: these offsprings have we made for you; accept them. So come to us with most auspicious favour: bestow on us unfailing health and plenty.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Bending the knee, sitting down on the right, let all assent to
    (abhi-gс╣Ы) this libation of ours; injure us not, O Fathers, by reason
    of any offense (─Б╠Бgas) which we may do to you through humanity.
Notes

That is, through human frailty. The corresponding RV. verse (x. 15. 6)
reads for b im├бс╣Б yaj├▒├бm abh├н gс╣Ыс╣З─лta v├н┼Ыve; and VS. (xix. 62)
agrees with RV.; the comm., too, so far as to have gс╣Ыс╣З─лta. In K─Бu┼Ы.
(83. 28), the verse accompanies the arranging of the bone relics of the
deceased at their place of burial (repeated, with two other verses, in
the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a, 87. 28). The Anukr. takes no notice of the
redundant syllable in b.

Griffith

Bowing their bended knees and seated southward let all accept this sacrifice with favour. Punish us not for any sin, O fathers which we through human frailty have committed.

релрей рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджреБрд╣рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╡рд╣рддреБрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Tvashс╣нar makes a wedding-car for his daughter; by reason of this,
    all this creation comes together; the mother of Yama, wife of great
    Vivasvant, being drawn about, disappeared.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 17. 1) has ├нti for t├йna at beginning
of b; and the comm. also reads iti. With the first half-verse
compare iii. 31. 5 a, b, which is a sort of travesty of it. The
second verse of the curious and obscure and much discussed (see
Bloomfield in JAOS. xv. 172 ff.) bit of legend is found below, as 2. 33,
as much out of all connection with its surroundings as this one here.
Neither of the two is used by K─Бu┼Ы. or V─Бit. The comm. quotes a passage
of eight verses from the Bс╣Ыhaddevat─Б in explanation of the legend.

Griffith

Tvashtar prepares the bridal for his daughter: therefore the whole of this our world assembles. But Yama’s mother, spouse of great Vivasvan, vanished as she was carried to her dwelling.

Translation
  1. Go thou forth, go forth by roads that go to the stronghold
    (p┼лry─Б╠Бс╣Зa), as (y├йn─Б) thy Fathers of old went forth; both kings,
    reveling with svadh─Б╠Б, shalt thou see, Yama and god Varuс╣Зa.

Griffith

Go forth, go forth upon the homeward pathways whither our sires of old have gone before us. Then shalt thou look on both the Kings enjoying their sacred food, God Varuna and Yama.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go ye away, go asunder, and creep apart from here; for this man the
    Fathers have made this world; adorned with days, with waters, with rays
    (akt├║), a rest (avas─Б╠Бna) Yama gives to him.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 14. 9, without variant; and TA. (in i. 27. 5; vi. 6.

  1. has the first, third, and fourth p─Бdas; while VS. (xii. 45) and TS.
    (in iv. 2. 4┬╣), TB. (i. 2. 1┬╣тБ╢), and MS. (ii. 7. 11), have only the
    first (agreeing with TA. in the second). TA., however, reads dad─Бtv
    av-     in d, and that is found also in our P.M.I. The comm. has for
    b the p─Бda of the other texts: ye тАШtra stha pur─Бс╣З─Б ye ca n┼лtan─Бс╕е.
    тМКMy discussion of the verse in Skt. Reader, p. 378, may be consulted.тМЛ
    The verse, with 2. 37, accompanies in K─Бu┼Ы. (So. 42) the sprinkling of
    the place of cremation with holy water; in V^ait. (28. 24), the sweeping
    of the site for the householder’s fire, in the agnicayana ceremony.
    тМКWeber, Sb. 1895, p. 839, takes the verse as a call, addressed to all
    creatures (whether animals or demons) that may infest the resting-place
    of the dead man, to quit the same (averruncatio).тМЛ

Griffith

Go hence, depart ye, fly in all directions. This world for him the Fathers have provided. Yama bestow upon this man a dwelling adorned with days and beams of light and waters.

Griffith

Our Fathers are Angirases, Navagvas, Atharvans, Bhrigus, who deserve the Soma. May these, the holy, look on us with favour; may we enjoy their gracious loving-kindness.

Translation
  1. These ascended up from here; they ascended the backs of the sky
    (d├нv); the An╠Дgirases have gone forth to heaven (d├нv), like
    bh┼лrj├нs, by the road.

does our edition; but the mss. decidedly favor ├║d ─Б╠Б тАЩruhan (p. ├║t: ─Б╠Б:
aruhan), and SPP. rightly adopts this reading. The comm. reads etad

bh┼лс╕е: j├бyah, this pada-text dividing compound words without any
hyphen or its equivalent between the parts) an epithet of the An╠Дgirases,
rendering it by bharaс╣Зavanto bhuvaс╣Б jitavanto v─Б, and justifies the

Griffith

He hath gone hence and risen on high mounting heaven’s ridges by that path Whereon the sons of Angiras, the conquerors of earth, went up.

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: ремрезтИТ(рдЗрддрдГ) (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН)рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рддреНред рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрджрд╢рд╛рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН (рдПрддреЗ) рдкрд┐рддрд░рдГ (рдЙрддреН) рдЙрддреНрддрдорддрдпрд╛ (рдЖ рдЕрд░реБрд╣рдиреН) рдЖрд░реВрдврд╛ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп (рдкреГрд╖реНрдард╛рдирд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЖ рдЕрд░реБрд╣рдиреН) (рдкреНрд░) рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг (рднреВрд░реНрдЬрдпрдГ) рднреВ рд╕рддреНрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН-рд░реБрдХреНред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗред рдкрд╛реж рейредреиредренрелред рдЬрд┐ рдЬрдпреЗ-рд╡рд┐рдЪреНредрднреВрд░реНрднреБрд╡реЛ рднреВрдореЗрд░реНрдЬреЗрддрд╛рд░рдГ (рдпрдерд╛) рд╕рд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпреЗ (рдкрдерд╛) рд╕рдиреНрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг (рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдореН (рдЕрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд┐рдирдГ (рдпрдпреБрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреБрдГ рее
